Guangdong Province Transportation Construction: Survey of Funds for Construction of the Southern Section of the Yuehan Railway; Southwest Civil Aviation Company Adds Guangzhou-Babu Line

Guangzhou Communication: Guangdong Province has been actively engaged in transportation construction recently, with particular attention to highway administration and aviation. Currently, the Yuehan Railway Southern Section Bureau is both handling responsible transport and accelerating the construction of railway tracks in the Xiang-Yue border region. Due to the vastness of the project and the presence of overlapping mountains above Lechang Pingshi, construction is particularly difficult, resulting in significant costs. According to statistics from the Railway Bureau, the operation of the Shao-Le section (i.e., from Shaozhou to Lechang) of the Yuehan Railway is mostly funded by the Belgian Boxer Indemnity for purchasing materials, approximately 2.7 million yuan in national currency. The next largest source is funds allocated by the Yuehan Railway Southern Section Bureau on behalf of the Ministry, amounting to over 2.4 million yuan in national currency. Thirdly, over 800,000 yuan in cash and over 300,000 yuan in materials have been allocated from the British Boxer Indemnity. Additionally, the Ministry of Railways has allocated over 280,000 yuan in cash, totaling approximately 6.7 million yuan. The construction materials and labor costs for the Zhu-Le section (i.e., from Lechang to Zhuzhou) are almost entirely funded by the British Boxer Indemnity, including 1.66 million pounds of material funds arriving in London, 1.24 million pounds of labor funds arriving in China, and 1.25 million pounds of undated public bonds. (The original amount of the undated bonds was 1.56 million pounds, but 1.5 million pounds were issued at a 90% discount, resulting in the actual receipt of the above amount). With the exception of a small portion of material funds used for the Shao-Le section, the total is over 4.2 million British pounds, approximately equivalent to 60 million yuan in national currency. In recent years, the low price of the British pound has significantly affected the adequacy of construction and material funds. The Ministry of Railways has had to find other ways to make up the shortfall. Additionally, the Yuehan Railway Southern Section Bureau has provided a subsidy of over 100,000 yuan. The above is the recent situation regarding the construction of the southern section of the Yuehan Railway. In terms of aviation, the Southwest Civil Aviation Company is currently planning to open additional air routes to facilitate inter-provincial transportation and communication. Recently, it has been actively establishing the Guang-Gan line, from Guangzhou to Ganxian. Furthermore, it is planning the Liang-Guang Eight Line, from Guangzhou to Babu in Guangxi. The Guangzhou-Wuzhou route has been operating for a long time, but because Wuzhou is located upstream of the Xijiang River, civil aviation aircraft only reach Yonggui and other places. However, Babu in Guangxi Province is connected to the Xiaobeijiang River in Guangdong Province, and land and water transportation in the area is inconvenient. Therefore, the Guang-Ba Civil Aviation Line is being opened to facilitate rapid transportation. Personnel have been dispatched to Babu and Hexian in Guangxi and Xiaobeijiang in Guangdong to survey locations and construct airfields. On the other hand, civil aviation aircraft have been ordered from foreign companies in Hong Kong. If they can be delivered on schedule, Guangzhou and Babu can officially open air service in January of next year. (December 22)

Land Consolidation in Jiangxi Province —The First Phase Completed—

Nanchang Dispatch: The land tax in various counties of this province has been levied according to the fixed quotas of the former Qing Dynasty. There have been numerous malpractices, such as land without tax, tax without land, secret abandonment, and new ownership without old taxation. Since the provincial government ordered the Department of Finance to actively consolidate, such as abolishing excessive levies, collecting arrears, and establishing charitable lands, the accumulated malpractices have gradually been eliminated and the results are remarkable. However, these measures are still passive. The active aspect must start with land consolidation, because without implementing land consolidation and assessing prices per mu, it would be difficult to reduce the burden on ordinary people and increase the province's revenue. Therefore, the provincial government established a Land Consolidation Bureau the year before last, planning to consolidate the land throughout the province, and decided on eleven counties, including Nanxin, as the first phase. The Land Consolidation Bureau has now been renamed the Land Bureau, and it is still proceeding according to the original plan. After this consolidation of land in various counties, Nanchang, Xinjian, Anyi, Fengcheng, Jinxian, Linchuan, Nanfeng, and other counties have all successively completed the process. According to the results of the consolidation in each county, Nanchang has exceeded the original farmland by approximately 100,000 mu, Xinjian by more than 300,000 mu, Anyi by 120,000 mu, and Fengcheng by 600,000 mu. Based on this extrapolation, the 83 counties in the province are expected to exceed a huge number of ten million to thirty million mu. There are two reasons for the increase: one is that in the past, wealthy families possessed land without paying taxes, and the other is that newly owned land has not been taxed. After this consolidation, the malpractices of land without tax and tax without land can be eliminated, and the burden on ordinary people can be directly reduced. Because in the future, a land value tax will be implemented, and all land will be taxed according to its value, and corrupt and powerful officials will have no way to practice their cunning. As for the method of land declaration in this province, it is said that it will be implemented soon. (25th)

Songjiang: Inmates Transferred from Prison Bully New Inmates

Since the county prison began housing opium offenders, it has become increasingly overcrowded due to the narrowness of the prison cells. Even the corridors are crowded with many people, suffering from the elements. Previously, thirty strong inmates were transferred and detained in the detention center of the local court. Unexpectedly, these transferred inmates have been extremely oppressive to the new inmates, and there have been repeated reports of this. Recently, Xia Buying, who was detained for civil reasons, was bullied, threatened, and injured by eleven transferred inmates, including Jiang Tang. The incident was heard by the judge, who personally investigated and sent the eleven inmates, including Jiang, back to the main prison.

Jiading: Gu Weijun Returns to Native Place to Bury Brother

Gu Weijun, the ambassador to France, lost his elder brother, Weiqing, to illness on the 12th of last month at his residence at 220 Macdonnell Road, Shanghai. On the 25th of this month, a memorial service and family worship were held. Xu Cixuan, the county magistrate of this county, made a special trip to Shanghai to express his condolences. On the morning of the 26th, Ambassador Gu, along with his nephews Shan Chang, Ying Chang, Hai Chang, and nieces Jun Qi and Jun Liang, escorted the coffin back to their hometown, taking a Shanghai-Taicang bus to Panjiaqiao Station. Magistrate Xu dispatched a platoon of security guards and police officers to protect them. The cemetery is located in Mengjin Township, the third district of the county. After arriving at the station, they transferred to a boat to transport the coffin to the cemetery, arriving at noon. Ambassador Gu inspected the site and returned to his Shanghai residence at 2 p.m. On the 27th, at the hour of Wei (1-3 p.m.), Ambassador Gu went to the cemetery from Shanghai to pay his respects again. According to Ambassador Gu's words to relatives and friends, the embassy building in France was originally rented, but now the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has approved the allocation of funds for construction to enhance the national prestige. He has been back in the country for thirteen months. He originally intended to go to France to take up his new post as ambassador as soon as possible, but he could not do so because his brother's funeral had not yet taken place. Once the funeral is completed, he must leave the country and take up his post in mid-January next year, he said.

Changshu: Eurasia Airplane Forced to Land

Eurasia Aviation's No. 16 mail plane, which flew from Zhengzhou to Shanghai the day before yesterday, passed through Yiyi around 5 p.m. After the New Year, due to the adverse weather conditions after the snow, it could not proceed and was forced to land in the area of Yin Jingzhang in Shizhuang, east of Tianmo City. The aircraft was slightly damaged. Fortunately, the two pilots, both women, and an interpreter were unharmed. They learned from the bus station that they were running out of fuel, so they urgently dispatched a car to provide gasoline. A Chinese interpreter arrived in the city and telegraphed the Shanghai company, requesting them to send someone to Changshu to repair the plane and transport it to Shanghai. Later, the two pilots went to Tianshenggang at 10 a.m. on the 26th. The Yamato ship happened to be sailing from Shanghai, and the students boarded the ship, instructing it to sail directly to Nanjing. Xu Zhen, the special commissioner of the Nantong district, Jin Zonghua, the county magistrate, Song Mingqi, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, and Yao Gen, the director of education, received the news and went to the port to dissuade them. The students were very determined, and the situation remained deadlocked until night. All the Jianglun ships going up and down the river were temporarily suspended.

Educational Broadcasting Column

Lecture on National Language Studies What to Read (Continued)

—Xia Gaizun, Director of the Editorial Department of Kaiming Bookstore

Next, let's talk about reference books. If any of you ask me what reference books you should read for a certain subject, I honestly cannot answer. I believe that the need for reference books arises from specific topics, and it is temporary and cannot be decided in advance. To put it bluntly, for those who read the first type of books carelessly, there is no need for reference books at all. You must have a topic to consult a reference book. If you don't have a specific topic in mind, flipping through a book randomly is a meaningless and silly thing, like randomly flipping through a dictionary when you don't want to look up a word. Taking the National Language Studies as an example, if you read "Peach Blossom Spring" in the National Language textbook and there are words you don't understand, you have to look them up in the dictionary. At this time, the dictionary (assuming it is the "Ciyuan") becomes a reference book. This article ("Peach Blossom Spring") was written by a Jin Dynasty person. If you feel that the sentiment is somewhat different from the articles written by people from other eras, and you want to know about the situation of Jin Dynasty literature, you will flip through the "History of Chinese Literature" (assuming it is the "History of Chinese Literature" compiled by Xie Wuliang). At this time, the "History of Chinese Literature" becomes your reference book. This article describes a kind of utopian thought. You have learned from teachers and friends that there is a social thinker named Thomas More in England who wrote a book called "Utopia," which is similar in nature to what Tao Qian wrote. If you take it out for comparison, "Utopia" becomes your reference book. This article belongs to the narrative category. If you want to understand the format of narrative essays, you will flip through "How to Write Narrative Essays" (assuming it is compiled by Sun Liangong). At this time, "How to Write Narrative Essays" becomes your reference book. Also, the author of this article is called Tao Qian. If you want to know about his character, you will flip through "Biography of Tao Qian in the Book of Jin" or "The Collected Works of Tao". At this time, "The Book of Jin" or "The Collected Works of Tao" becomes your reference book. These many reference books only arise when there is a topic. Without a topic, there is no way to consult a reference book. Although the school library has many books, and although you actually have many books, they are useless. It is the same with other subjects as it is with National Language Studies. If you are in a history class and listen to the teacher lecturing on the Industrial Revolution in England, if you have a question about this historical event that you want to investigate, you must ask the teacher for many reference books. The library has books on English history, various economic books, and single articles published in recent magazines that are related to this event, all of which become your reference books. Therefore, I believe that reference books cannot be listed in advance. You can only decide temporarily according to the topic you want to consult. Before going to the library to find reference books, first ask yourself, what is the topic I want to consult? If you have a topic but don't know what books to find, you can ask the teacher, ask your friends, and check the book catalog. The worst thing is not even having a topic.

What I said above is about reference books. Next, I will talk about the third type of books, which are books on cultivating interests. These books can be said to be unrelated to schoolwork, and you can choose them entirely according to your own preferences and needs. A person's interests will change. Someone who likes drawing for a while may soon like music. Someone who likes literature may later like religion. As for the cultivation aspect, it is even broader, and the changes are even more numerous. At some point, you may learn that your own shortcomings are in aspect A and should be supplemented and corrected. After a while, you may feel that your shortcomings are in aspect B and should be supplemented and corrected. These natural changes should not be forced or constrained. It is best not to change the goal during a certain period. Reading Tao's poems this week and the history of Western painting next week will make it impossible to cultivate your interests. Reading Zeng Guofan's family letters this week and Cheng Yi's Analects next week will make it difficult to achieve the effect of cultivation. Therefore, I believe that the number of books of this kind does not need to be large in the same period, but the selection should be refined. Select one or two types and set aside time to read them well. Suppose you have decided on a certain type of book on interests and a certain type of book on cultivation for this semester, you may as well just read them. Read them in your spare time outside of regular classes, read them on Sundays, read them after finishing your daily homework, read them on the train or boat when traveling, and read them while sitting on the grass when strolling in the park. If you are not tired of reading them by the end of the semester, continue reading them again next semester until you are tired of them. You may be surprised to hear what I have said. I dare not deceive you. Your purpose in reading this type of book is not to pass the exam, nor is it to graduate sooner or later, but entirely for your own benefit. It is entirely up to you whether you read a book for a year or half a year. The only thing that matters is that it benefits you, and there is no need to worry about the length of time. It is meaningful to read your favorite books permanently. Zhao Pu's reading of the Analects is a famous historical story in China. There was a Japanese writer named Tsubouchi Shoyo, who recently died. He lived for more than eighty years, but he read Shakespeare's plays for more than fifty years.

My words are finished. Now let's have a conclusion. I believe that books are a tool for providing knowledge, and reading is a means of improving and enriching life. What books to read should be decided and selected according to life. First, you should read books about your job, second, reference books, and third, books about cultivating interests. Middle school students should first read the textbooks carefully, because the job of middle school students is to study the middle school curriculum. Reference books can be decided according to the topic you want to consult. The most important thing is to discover the topic. As for books on cultivating interests, you can choose freely. The number of types does not need to be large, the selection should be refined, and you should only change them when you are tired of reading them. (The End)

Local News

Petitioning Students Return to Shanghai from Wuxi. Disembarked at Nanxiang around 6 PM Last Night. The Municipal Government Provided Cars to Transport Them Back to School. Traffic on the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway Expected to Be Smooth in the Coming Days.

The student delegation of Fudan University and other schools, totaling more than 1,680 students, who went to Nanjing to petition this month, arrived at Wuxi at dawn the day before yesterday, after which Gu Zhenglun, the Nanjing Garrison Commander, arrived in Wuxi and, together with representatives from the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Education, conveyed President Chiang's wishes. However, the student delegation insisted on continuing westward by train, so the Railway Bureau had no choice but to dismantle the tracks to stop them. Yesterday (the 27th) at dawn, the student delegation finally complied with the advice and disembarked at Wuxi Station with flags lowered. They were invited by the Military Police Commander Gu Zhenglun and the Wuxi County Magistrate Long Tiyao to enter Wuxi County and paraded around the city once before entering the Zhongnan Grand Theater to concentrate on listening to instructions. The student delegation publicly elected Fudan as the student representative to preside over the ceremony and order of the entire venue. Garrison Commander Gu also read out a telegram from President Chiang, expressing his deep approval of the students' enthusiasm for patriotism, and earnestly advised the students that patriotism must follow the right path to prevent being taken advantage of. Ma Zongrong, the Secretary-General of the Ministry of Education, also read out a telegram from Minister Wang. Finally, Pan Gongzhan, the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, spared no effort in persuading the students to return to Shanghai. The student delegation, feeling that the authorities were so sincere in conveying their petitioning purpose to the central government, reluctantly agreed to return to Shanghai that day. Around 3 PM, the student delegation reorganized and boarded the original train. Around 6 PM that day, they arrived in Nanxiang. Upon disembarking, the Shanghai Municipal Government had already hired a large number of cars to welcome them at the station. The male and female student delegations had been suffering from hunger and cold for days, and many had not been able to wash, so they all looked haggard, but their spirits were still very strong. In the area around the North Station, the military and police had all withdrawn around 6 PM and were replaced by armed road police to maintain order. The situation was no longer as tense as it had been in the previous two days. However, the North Station has not yet announced the lifting of martial law because it has been designated as a martial law zone, so passengers cannot pass through. Instead, they change trains at Nanxiang, Macdonnell Road, and the Upper West and Upper South Stations. The detailed situation is recorded as follows:

Staying Overnight at Gaoqiao. More than 1,000 students from Fudan University, Fudan Affiliated Middle School, Fudan Experimental School, Jianguo Middle School, New Asia Middle School, Huanghuagang Middle School, North Municipal Middle School, Law School, and other schools in the city who went to Beijing to petition, left Shanghai on the 24th on two trains. After arriving in Kunshan, except for one train of Tongji students, who were persuaded by the authorities and returned to Shanghai on the 25th, the remaining train continued westward. When passing through Suzhou and Wuxi, many sections of the track were dismantled, so a patrol team of ten students was organized to lead the way on handcars, repairing the tracks at any time. On the 26th, they arrived at Gaoqiao, west of Wuxi, but the rails on the bridge had been dismantled and could not be repaired, so they stayed overnight in the train there.

Leaving Wuxi to Return to Shanghai. Yesterday at 4 AM, the authorities sent personnel to Gaoqiao to find a way to drive back to Wuxi. At that time, Duanmu Kai, a councilor of the Executive Yuan, Sun Guofeng, an inspector of the Ministry of Education, Ma Zongrong, a secretary, Gu Zhenglun, the Commander of the Capital Military Police, from Nanjing, and Pan Gongzhan, the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, and Li Dachao, the chief of the First Section of the Municipal Government, as well as principals, teachers, and staff from various schools in Shanghai, arrived one after another to persuade the students to get off the train and gather at the Zhongnan Grand Theater near the station. Long Tiyao, the county magistrate, took care of everything. After entering the theater, Duanmu, Sun, and others read out President Chiang's and Minister Wang's telegrams and persuaded them to return to school. After receiving the instructions, the students were quite moved and expressed their willingness to return to school. Therefore, at 3 PM, they boarded the train and left Wuxi to return to Shanghai.

Arriving Back in Nanxiang. After the student train departed from Wuxi Station at 3 PM, the first train was a security team train, and Li Dachao, the chief of the First Section of the Municipal Government, was also on board. It drove eastward first, followed by the student train, which was divided into nine sections and drove in succession. At 5:40, the first train arrived in Nanxiang first. Chief Li immediately ordered the security team to be on guard inside and outside Nanxiang Station, fully protecting them. Around 6 PM, the student train also arrived. In addition to Chief Li of the Municipal Government taking care of them at the station, Zhang Xiaotong, sent by the Municipal Party Headquarters, also led the staff to take care of everything at the station.

Transported Back to School Separately. At this time, the municipal government had sent a large number of cars to stop outside the station. The staff sent by the Municipal Party Headquarters went to each section of the train to greet the students one by one. The students were still very energetic in the train, shouting slogans and singing majestic patriotic songs, but there were some who looked tired. The students got off the train in batches, lined up at the station, and after leaving the station, they boarded the cars and were sent back to their respective schools. A small number of students were still on the original train because the cars were not enough to distribute them. They drove straight to Jiangwan. At 9:55, they passed the North Station and arrived in Jiangwan at 10:10. In total, it took four days and nights on the road from the departure on the afternoon of the 23rd to 9 PM last night, which is the end of this stage.

Welcome from Schoolmates. The students of various schools who stayed in Shanghai, after hearing the news that the petitioning students had accepted the advice and returned to Shanghai, went to Nanxiang Station yesterday afternoon to welcome them. Such as the Fudan Alumni Association and the Nankai University students, all went to comfort them. The authorities of Fudan, Jianguo, Southeast, Zhengfeng, and other schools all specially prepared vehicles yesterday evening to welcome them.

Sun and Hao Report to the Ministry. Sun Guofeng and Hao Gengsheng, the representatives of the Ministry of Education, telegraphed to the Ministry of Education last night after escorting the students back to Shanghai, saying: Respectfully to the Vice Minister of Education in Nanjing. At 3 PM today, we escorted all the students back to Shanghai from Wuxi. They arrived safely in Nanxiang at 9 PM. They have now been sent back to their respective schools by car. The result was unexpectedly satisfactory. We plan to take the night train back to Beijing to report in detail. Respectfully, Feng, Su, and Kou are grateful.

The Ministry of Education Urges Li. Yesterday, Fudan University received a telegram from Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education, which read: To Principal Li, recently, we received your respectful telegram delivered by the Executive Yuan on the Respect Day, and we learned about your painstaking efforts to maintain school discipline these days, and we are very grateful. We sincerely hope that you will find a way to continue to persuade the students on the way to return to school and not have any thoughts of retreat. This is what we pray for. Your brother Wang Shijie You.

Passenger Trains Resume. Yesterday, traffic on the two lines has mostly resumed, but Shanghai North Station is still under partial martial law, and passengers cannot enter the station to purchase tickets and board trains. Therefore, passengers traveling up the Nanjing-Shanghai Line must board at Nanxiang Station, and passengers traveling down must disembark at Macdonnell Road Station. Passengers traveling up and down the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Line must board and disembark at the Southwest Stations. After 6 PM yesterday, all trains arriving in Shanghai on both lines could directly reach the North Station. From 8 AM this morning, all passenger trains on both lines completely resumed their original state.

A Letter from Old Man Ninety-Six to the Students of Fudan University.

After the news that the students of Fudan University were prevented from going to Beijing to petition spread, Mr. Ma Xiangbo, the founder of the school, who is now ninety-six years old, was very concerned. Now we have found his letter to the students of the school as follows: Students of Fudan University, in recent days you have been rushing about for the sake of the national crisis, braving the wind and dew, and not even having time to sleep. I am very gratified to hear this. However, Principal Li Denghui has resigned because of this, which makes me feel anxious. However, Principal Li's strong advice to you not to go to Nanjing is indeed to the point, because the officials of the government are all naturally intelligent and must have thought about it carefully and planned thoroughly. (Omission)

Therefore, your trip to Nanjing, even if it becomes a reality, will be meaningless. However, the cornerstone of the country lies in the people. The root cause of today's phenomenon of national subjugation lies first in the ignorance of the people. Look at other civilized countries, are there such situations? The reason for this can be deeply considered. For your sake, instead of appealing to the government, it is better to enlighten the people. Streets and alleys, teahouses and taverns, are all places where you can exert your strength for the country. You must make them clearly aware of their own strength and responsibility, take up their weapons and rise up, and work together to move forward. Then what you do to fulfill your duties is also to supplement the government's education efforts where they are lacking. As an old man, I cannot share your hardships, so I offer my humble opinion. I hope you will strive for the country and cherish yourselves. Ma Xiangbo, December 27, 24th year of the Republic of China.

Real Estate Mortgage Loan Bank. The Ministry of Finance Orders Establishment. Orders the China Construction Bank to Prepare for Establishment.

Since the implementation of the legal currency, the Ministry of Finance has been actively planning to increase the number of real estate mortgage loan banks in order to promote the activity of real estate. It is now heard that the Ministry of Finance has designated experts to draft a plan and ordered the China Construction Bank to plan for its establishment. The letter from the Ministry of Finance is recorded as follows: This Ministry has stated in the case of implementing the legal currency that it will establish a real estate mortgage loan bank to promote the vigor of the market, etc., which has been announced to the public. For more than a month, this Ministry has designated experts to draft a plan and discussed it with various parties, and a rough outline has been formed. However, this bank is very important in terms of domestic and foreign credit. The company has many dealings with foreign financial circles and has always been reputable. It is hereby ordered that the company immediately follow the company's management to plan for the establishment of a real estate mortgage loan bank. All capital accounting shall be divided independently from the company, and this Ministry will separately promote the raising of share capital to enrich its strength and facilitate its progress. Immediately prepare for its establishment and report the date of establishment. This order.

This City's Petitioning Students Return to Shanghai Schools; Mayor Wu Reissues a Letter to Students: Passion Runs High: How Can I Contain Myself? I Offer Sincere Words: Urgently and Earnestly Conveying Them

Following the return of petitioning students from this city last night, Mayor Wu Tiecheng has reissued a sincere letter to the students. The original text is as follows: The petitioning students from this city, excluding those from Tongji and other schools who had already arrived in Shanghai from Kunshan the previous evening, were, after earnest persuasion by the central and Shanghai educational authorities, transported back to Shanghai from Wuxi at 3 PM yesterday. Upon the return of you all, Tiecheng feels as if a loving mother has been reunited with her beloved children; passion runs high, how can I contain myself? Therefore, I offer my sincere words and earnestly, with tears, convey them to all the students of our city.

Since the proposal to petition in Beijing was initiated, you gathered at the North Station, crowding the train cars. In those train cars, did you ever consider the treacherous atmosphere inside and outside the North Station, and throughout the entire city of Shanghai? Your patriotism is, of course, genuine, and your spirit and passion should be sympathized with and admired by us and the people of the entire nation. However, China faces many difficulties, and the situation is complex. The environment in Shanghai is particularly unique. How could we know that those deranged and wicked individuals would seize the opportunity to manipulate public sentiment in order to achieve their sinister plot of using the youth to create chaos? From the second day you arrived at the station, the number of people surged to four or five thousand, and at the same time, reactionary leaflets were frequently discovered. In the Shishan Road area, there were over a thousand people preparing to gather, and some were even willing to create disturbances at all costs, hoping to cause tragedies and brew significant changes. At the time, the situation was perilous and the public was in a state of panic. Tiecheng does not wish to give a detailed account of this. He is only mindful that our bright and promising youth are in this treacherous and unpredictable environment, and if we do not make early and appropriate plans to ensure your safety, the situation will become unimaginable. Therefore, in addition to finding ways to persuade some students to leave the station and return to school, to protect you all and devise a foolproof plan for you, we had no choice but to move the train away from the North Station to avoid unforeseen circumstances. This is the painstaking effort Tiecheng made to protect the youth and maintain the safety of the city, which should be understood by all citizens of our city.

Since you departed from the station and headed west, the Shanghai Municipal Government, in addition to immediately dispatching responsible personnel to rush ahead on different routes to provide careful care, also immediately dispatched personnel to your respective school authorities to go and assist in persuasion and comfort. As for Tiecheng, he was restless from morning till night, from dusk till dawn, and never ceased for a moment to be concerned about your food, clothing, warmth, and living arrangements. He also dispatched the Director of Education and others to persuade on his behalf.

Fortunately, one train of Tongji and other schools returned to Shanghai the previous evening, and the classmates who were stranded in Wuxi also arrived completely last night. This humble sincerity should be understood and accepted by all the students of our city.

You have all returned to school. Although you did not reach Beijing, responsible representatives from the ministries in Beijing have already met with you many times. Although your petitioning train did not reach Beijing, your petitioning will has long been forwarded by the Municipal Government and has been commended and accepted by the central authorities. Your petitioning spirit, as well as your spirit of striving for the country with perseverance and determination, have already been admired and emulated by the people of the entire nation. Return, students! You should restrain yourselves a little, appreciate the sincerity of your teachers' love and care, and quietly contemplate the path of truly serving the country in the future.

Regarding the opinion of how the youth of today should serve the country, Tiecheng has already made a sincere and earnest declaration on the 21st of this month, which will not be repeated here. However, if we truly have a deep understanding of the national crisis, we should realize that the true way to serve the country today is not through momentary indignation, but through permanent struggle; not through momentary passion, but through diligence in one's position. If we allow emotions to cloud our reason, mistake the superficial for the real, and mistake means for ends, then we will be eager for quick success but fail to achieve it, and we will move further away from the path of national revival. Throughout the history of national salvation movements, there has been one most tragic phenomenon: the misuse of power and the mutual cancellation of power, which has not only failed to help the national crisis but has also harmed the vitality of society. This is what those who truly love the country are most saddened by. Our country is inherently a nation rich in ability. If our awakened youth can avoid the superficial and unrealistic mistakes of past national salvation movements, recognize the root causes of the national crisis, and understand the overall needs of the nation, then each of us should strive in our respective positions, contribute our abilities, deeply understand the relationship of interdependence, uphold the spirit of being in the same boat, and work together as one, united from top to bottom. We should strive with sincerity, avoid internal strife, and vow to fight for the survival of the nation under the leadership of the central government and within the discipline of the entire nation. Then, even with our deep-rooted weakness, every effort we make will alleviate the national crisis by one point. As a result of the concerted efforts and sincere unity of the entire nation, we will surely create an immeasurably great national power and glorify the long and great life of our Chinese nation.

The national crisis has not yet ended, and the world is changing rapidly. Return, students! Let us encourage each other.

December 27, 1935, in Shanghai.

The Special District Court's Agreement Expires in April of Next Year

Our Ministry of Foreign Affairs has notified all relevant groups.

The Legal Rights Research Association will hold a meeting soon to discuss measures.

Regarding the agreement on the Shanghai Special District Court, which will expire on April 1st of next year, a reporter from the Jiji News Agency, in order to understand whether the agreement will be extended after its expiration, or whether it will be abolished and new measures will be planned, inquired about the details from people in the judicial field and recorded them as follows:

Agreement Process: The Concession Court Agreement was signed in Nanjing in 1930 (the 19th year of the Republic of China) by representatives of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and representatives of five countries, including Britain, the United States, the Netherlands, Norway, and Brazil. France signed as a supplement later. As a result, the Jiangsu Shanghai Special District Local Court (i.e., the First and Second Special District Courts) and the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court in the Shanghai Public Concession were established on April 1st of that year (i.e., the date the agreement became effective). This was the process of recovering the Mixed Court and reorganizing to establish the court.

Extension for Three Years: The original term of the agreement was three years, expiring on April 1st, 1933 (the 22nd year of the Republic of China). However, it was noted in the agreement and attached exchange of notes that the term could be extended with the consent of both parties after its expiration. Therefore, upon its expiration that year, after consultation between our Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the relevant countries, it was decided to extend it for three years, expiring on April 1st, 1936 (the 25th year of the Republic of China).

After Expiration: According to the provisions of the extended agreement, notification should be given to the other party (i.e., the relevant countries) six months before the expiration date, otherwise it should continue to be effective until one party notifies the other party of cancellation and six months have passed. The reporter from the Jiji News Agency learned that our Ministry of Foreign Affairs has notified the relevant countries, but it is not yet clear what measures will be taken.

Active Research: The judicial authorities in our country believe that this matter is of great importance and have now authorized the Legal Rights Research Committee to study the measures, which will then be provided to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for future negotiations. Qin Zhen, Vice President of the Judicial Yuan, has scheduled to return to Beijing the day after tomorrow to convene the Legal Rights Research Association to discuss everything in order to decide on measures as soon as possible. It is said that the agreement will be largely revised based on the original text.

Tang Youren's Coffin Closing This Afternoon; Central Political Council Representative Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning with Condolence Money; Mrs. Tang Telegraphed Thanks to President Jiang of the Executive Yuan for Condolences

Tang Youren, former Permanent Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs and current Permanent Vice Minister of Communications and Advisor to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, was shot and killed by thugs. After his body was moved to the Shanghai Funeral Home, the coffin will be closed this afternoon at 2 PM. Tang's brother, Kui Liang, rushed to Shanghai last night. Yang Zijing, a representative of the Central Political Council, arrived in Shanghai by ship yesterday morning, bringing condolence money of 3,000 yuan. In addition to Mrs. Wang and Mr. Chu Minyi representing Chairman Wang of the Central Political Council to express condolences, Chairman Wang also sent a personal letter to Mrs. Tang yesterday to express condolences. Those who went to express condolences yesterday included envoys and consuls from various countries. Condolence telegrams continue to arrive in Shanghai from various parties. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Coffin Closing This Afternoon: Mr. Tang's remains are scheduled to be placed in the coffin at 2 PM this afternoon. The ceremony will be simple at that time, with only friends from all parties participating in the public memorial. The obituary from the Tang residence is recorded as follows: Mr. Tang Youren was shot and seriously injured by thugs in his Shanghai residence at 5 PM on December 25th and passed away. The coffin will be closed at the Shanghai Funeral Home on Xujiahui Road at 2 PM on December 28th. Respectfully announced by the Tang Residence Funeral Committee.

Issuance of Condolence Money: The Central Political Committee issued condolence money of 3,000 yuan as temporary expenses for Mr. Tang's funeral. Mr. Yang Zijing, a representative of the Secretariat of the Central Political Council, was sent to handle Mr. Tang's funeral. Due to the train being impassable and the plane unavailable, he delayed until yesterday morning before taking a boat to Shanghai. The money has been brought by Mr. Yang.

Wang's Letter of Condolence: Chairman Wang Jingwei of the Central Political Council only learned yesterday of the tragic news of Tang Youren's assassination and was deeply grieved and indignant. He specially wrote a letter to Mrs. Tang to express his condolences. The original letter read: Mrs. Tang, upon learning of Mr. Youren's tragic death this morning, I was deeply grieved and indignant. Mr. Youren died for the country, worthy of the martyrs. I only hope that you will serve your elderly mother-in-law above and nurture your orphaned children below to comfort his spirit. I am confined by illness and unable to attend the memorial service in person. I write this letter with tears and know not what to say. Sincerely, Wang Zhaoming, December 27th.

Condolence Telegrams and Letters: Foreign Minister Zhang Qun telegraphed: I was shocked to hear of the death of my brother Youren, and I am deeply saddened. My sister-in-law must be deeply grieved by the profound affection between you and your husband. However, considering that the sudden change was extraordinary, I still pray that you restrain your grief and take care of yourself. Sincerely, Zhang Qun. Military and Political Minister He Yingqin telegraphed: I was deeply saddened and mourned to hear of my brother Youren's misfortune in Shanghai. I send this telegram to express my condolences. He Yingqin. Minister of the Interior Jiang Zobin telegraphed: I was deeply shocked and saddened to hear of the passing of Mr. Youren. I hope that you will restrain your grief and pray that you will not cause excessive grief to the elders. Jiang Zobin. Minister of Education Wang Shijie telegraphed: I was deeply saddened to hear of the passing of Mr. Youren and miss him endlessly. I sincerely pray that you will pay attention to the great responsibility of educating and nurturing your nephews and nieces, restrain your grief, and take good care of yourself. Wang Shijie Xiao Dehua. He Jian of the Hunan Provincial Government telegraphed: Mr. Youren diligently served the Party and the country and made outstanding contributions. We deeply admire and respect him as a fellow villager. The last time I was in Beijing, I spent a long time with him, and we had pleasant conversations. I recently heard that he was suddenly shot and killed by thugs in his Shanghai residence. He comes from a family of scholars and officials, with two generations of loyalty and martyrdom. Not only do the people of Hunan mourn him, but the entire country sighs in grief. Considering that his mother is old and his children are young, I hope you will alleviate your grief to comfort his spirit in the afterlife and focus on the responsibility of raising his children. I send this telegram to express my condolences. He Jian. Mayor Ma Chaojun of Nanjing telegraphed: Mr. Youren was loyal, diligent, courageous, and knowledgeable. In recent years, he has assisted in diplomacy and worked tirelessly. I was deeply saddened to hear of his sudden death. I think of his aged mother and young children and hope that he will restrain his grief to assist in the major affairs. I hereby send my condolences. Shanghai Mayor Ma Chaojun. Jiang Mengling, President of Peking University, telegraphed: Mr. Youren suddenly suffered an accident and died. I am extremely saddened and grieved to hear the tragic news. I hereby send my condolences. Jiang Menglin. There were also condolence letters from Kong Xiangxi, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, Ye Chucang, Vice President of the Legislative Yuan, Tao Luqian, Vice Minister of the Interior, Zheng Lin, Vice Minister of Finance, Zeng Yangfu, Vice Minister of Railways, Shen Jinding, Minister to Panama, Tong Chaoqin, Consul General in San Francisco, Lu Bichou, former Vice Minister of Railways, Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, and Uchida Katsuji, President of the Japanese Toa Dobun Shoin, and a condolence letter from Li Zeyi, Advisor to the Fujian Provincial Government, totaling 56 items.

Student Patriotic Movement in Various Schools

Students of the Sino-French National Institute of Technology organized a National Salvation Committee and will start extensive publicity to all sectors today, on the 3rd.

The National Salvation Association of Jiangsu Provincial Wusong Fisheries School issued a notice, saying, "We are in the midst of deep water and fire, lamenting the daily decline of the country. We are deeply saddened. If we do not rise up to save ourselves, how can we survive? The students of our school, based on the principle that every person is responsible for the rise or fall of the nation, hereby make the following statements: 1. We vow to dedicate our lives to the country. 2. Eliminate traitors. 3. Please ask the government to make plans early to recover lost territories. 4. Oppose all puppet organizations. 5. We vow to use our blood to unite students across the country and engage in the national salvation movement. The oath has been made, and we will not look back. We will not hesitate to be crushed to pieces if the above points are not achieved. We hope you will observe this."

The Shanghai Municipal Secondary School Student National Salvation United Association held its second standing committee meeting yesterday. Jingye, Dagong, Minli Girls' High School, Youth, Junyi, Shanghai Girls' High School, Minguang, and others attended. Dagong was the chairman, and Wuben was the recorder. It was resolved that: 1. Dagong and Jingye schools were responsible for finding office locations. 2. The association's expenses were to be borne by each school at five yuan, which would be collected by the affairs section immediately. 3. St. John's Middle School was approved to join the association as a member. 4. News reporters would be summoned on a regular basis. 5. All standing committee members would represent the association to comfort the petitioning students from major middle schools in this city. 6. Representatives would be sent again to request the Municipal Education Bureau to withdraw its order to advance the New Year holiday. The meeting adjourned after discussion. The original letter of condolence to the petitioning students is recorded as follows: To the Shanghai Major Middle School Students Petitioning Delegation of Fudan University, we express our respects to the students who went to Beijing to petition in the midst of strong winds and heavy snow, promoting popular sentiment. We hereby extend our condolences and wish you good health. Initiated by the Shanghai Municipal Secondary School Student National Salvation United Association, this month's 24th. The students who gathered at the Shanghai Railway Station to go to Beijing to petition because the train was suspended, a portion of them left the station and departed that afternoon. In order to pass through the concession roads, North Henan Road and other places, all the iron gates there had been ordered closed by the concession police authorities. The students then detoured from Shishan Road into Beisichuan Road through Hanfu Lane. The reserve team defending that place, fearing that it would hinder order, also closed the iron gates there. Thereupon, a conflict arose between the two sides. A western patrolman, Lao Wu, was injured in the hand by a wooden stick, while a student, Wang Zhongguo, was detained. The student was only seventeen years old, a native of Wuxi, and a sophomore at Fudan High School. Yesterday morning, the police filed a public lawsuit with the First Special District Court under Article 136 of the Criminal Law. Judge Zhan then proposed an inquiry. First, patrolman Lao testified to the injury to his hand, and then Gu Youzhai, the Chinese patrolman of the Hongkou police station's reserve team, reported the circumstances of the arrest of the defendant. Questioned, the defendant confessed that because a female classmate fell to the ground at the time, he went to help her and was struck by a wooden stick and kicked. He then retaliated with his feet and did not use a stick to beat anyone. Judge Zhan reviewed the confession and, considering that the defendant was not yet an adult and his actions were excusable, leniently sentenced him to 15 days of detention and suspended the sentence for two years.

Fourteen Organizations Launch National Goods Sports Meet: Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday; Each Sponsoring Organization Appointed One Executive Committee Member; Organizational Draft Passed, Establishment on January 11th

Organizational Charter: Purpose: This association aims to unite various national goods organizations, engage in the study of the national goods movement of the Republic of China, Year 25, and implement practical and effective work to enhance the effectiveness of promoting national goods. Organization: This association is jointly organized by various national goods organizations in Shanghai and organizations that are enthusiastic about promoting or supporting national goods enterprises. Membership: Membership is based on each organization as a unit, and each organization may nominate three members. Staff: For the convenience of executing association affairs, each organization may nominate one executive committee member to form the executive committee. The executive committee may also hire individuals enthusiastic about promoting national goods to join as expert members or honorary members, and elect five standing committee members from the executive committee to handle daily affairs. Based on actual needs, employees may be hired to handle affairs. Work: The work to be undertaken by this association includes: Publicity, Lectures, Investigation, Exhibition, Research, Design, Statistics, Publication, Other. Association Affairs: The association affairs are provisionally divided into three departments: General Affairs Department, Foreign Department, Domestic Department. Each department is headed by one or two directors elected by the executive committee to manage the department's affairs. Meeting Schedule: The association holds a general membership meeting once per quarter and a committee meeting every two weeks, both convened by the standing committee members. Funding: The association's funding is shared by each organization or raised temporarily.

Currency Problem Solved: Shanghai-Sichuan Exchange Rate Stabilized; Only Five Yuan per Thousand from Shanghai to Sichuan; All Exchange Certificates Gradually Recalled

The six million yuan in local banknotes issued by Sichuan Province over the years, of which half was cash-backed and the remaining half was fully recovered by the Central Bank at 80% of its value, and the cash was returned to the state, caused a great panic regarding currency. Although the financial authorities planned to temporarily circulate a type of exchange certificate (totaling approximately nine million yuan), it was limited to Chongqing and was not a fundamental solution. Therefore, at the beginning of this month, Liu Hangchen, Director of the Sichuan Provincial Department of Finance, Guan Jiyu, Director of the Financial Supervision Office of the Military Affairs Commission, and Kang Xinru, General Manager of the Sichuan Meifeng Bank (representing Chongqing's financial community), flew to Shanghai together to consult with Finance Minister Kong about solutions. Kong approved an additional loan of eight million yuan from the Sichuan Post-Disaster Public Bonds. After the loan was secured, the three immediately returned to Sichuan. According to sources in Shanghai's Sichuan financial community, the loan has been allocated by the Chongqing branch of the Central Bank, with four million yuan loaned to the Sichuan Provincial Financial Authorities and four million yuan loaned to the Chongqing financial community. All previously circulating exchange certificates have been gradually recalled. As a result, the exchange rate between Shanghai and Chongqing has fallen from over one thousand and thirty yuan to five yuan per thousand, and between Shanghai and Chengdu to seven yuan per thousand. All are settled with legal tender as stipulated by the central government, with slightly higher interest rates. In this situation, Sichuan's finances are becoming increasingly stable.

Restaurants and Wine Shops to Collect Aviation Donations Starting January 15th Next Year; Collection Methods Submitted to the Municipal Government for Approval and Record

The Shanghai Collection Team Headquarters of the Chinese Aviation Association is launching a city-wide campaign to collect aviation donations from Chinese and Western restaurants and wine shops in order to raise funds for aviation and national salvation. Mr. Zhang Yuliang was appointed to liaise with the industry. A meeting was held on the 24th of this month on the ninth floor of the YMCA in Baxianqiao to discuss implementation. It was decided to collect one percent of the business income as a donation, with a target of 100,000 yuan, starting on January 15th of the 25th year of the Republic. It was reported in various newspapers that the office has formulated ten collection methods, which have been submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government for approval and record. A public announcement will be issued to inform the Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus. The collection methods are listed below: Regulations for the Collection of Aviation Donations from Shanghai's Restaurants and Wine Shops for National Salvation: 1. The Chinese Aviation Association formulates these regulations in order to raise aviation funds for national salvation. 2. All restaurants and wine shops, regardless of Chinese or Western, vegetarian or meat-based, banquets or snacks, are included in the collection. 3. All restaurants and wine shops will collect aviation donations at a rate of one percent (e.g., one cent for every yuan spent). Amounts under one yuan are exempt. Whether customers pay in cash or on account, the donation must be paid in cash. 4. The total amount of aviation donations collected from restaurants and wine shops is limited to 100,000 yuan. 5. All restaurants and wine shops must post the announcement and regulations for collecting aviation donations in the dining area or menu so that customers can read them. 6. Restaurants and wine shops must provide customers with a three-part receipt issued by the Chinese Aviation Association for the aviation donations collected. 7. Restaurants and wine shops must settle and submit the collected aviation donations every half month to the Shanghai Collection Team Headquarters of the Chinese Aviation Association. 8. The Chinese Aviation Association may send personnel to inspect the collection situation at any time after the aviation donation collection begins. If any irregularities are found, the government will be requested to take legal action. 9. The Chinese Aviation Association shall announce the amount of aviation donations collected from restaurants and wine shops monthly. 10. These regulations shall be implemented after being approved by the government.

Silk Cocoon Union Submits Request to Zhejiang Provincial Government to Improve Spring Cocoon Collection

Requests for Cocoon Merchants to Register in Three Phases; Overseas Silk Sales Showing Signs of Improvement; Government Agencies May No Longer Need to Operate Cocoon Collection

The Zhejiang Provincial Silk Cocoon Union, located on Rue Mère Lyautey in this city, submitted a request to the Zhejiang Provincial Government to improve spring cocoon collection next year. The document stated: "Submitted for suggestions for the 25th year:

Unified Management

Provisional measures for cocoon collection, draft proposal submitted for review and adoption. Zhejiang Province's silk industry is the best in Southeast China. Since the disastrous failure of the silk market, many sericulturists have suffered losses, and the silk industry's profits are hanging by a thread. The provincial government, sympathizing with the hardships of silkworm farmers, purchased and distributed improved silkworm eggs, guided improvements in sericulture, and implemented unified management of cocoon collection to prevent merchants from monopolizing and profiting. However, this session's

Too Strict Restrictions

Many cocoon businesses in various places that have the capital to collect cocoons have not been approved. In places where the establishment of cocoon businesses has not been allowed, silkworm farmers are suffering because there is no way to sell their cocoons. Both supply and demand sides are disappointed. Since autumn, silk sales have gradually improved, and the number of sericulturists next year will inevitably increase, and the amount of cocoons produced will also increase significantly. This association, for the convenience of

Silkworm Farmers Selling Cocoons

And for the sake of maintaining the affairs of the industry, after a joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees, a draft proposal for provisional measures for unified management of cocoon collection in the 25th year was formulated based on the provisional measures for unified management of cocoon collection in the autumn of the 24th year, with some revisions. The main points can be summarized into five items, which are presented as follows:

Overseas Silk Sales

Are gradually improving. Silk merchants have sufficient capital to collect cocoons, and government agencies may no longer need to operate cocoon collection to avoid people misunderstanding that the government is seizing business. The cocoon business registration period should be announced as soon as possible so that cocoon collection can be carried out according to registered and approved cocoon businesses to avoid unexpected losses. The registration period for cocoon merchants should be divided into

Phased Registration

The first phase is for local silk factories in the province to exercise their priority rights and be allowed to register without charge. The second phase is for registration by silk factories from other provinces. The third phase is for registration by other cocoon merchants. Local breeds should be allowed to be freely bought and sold by merchants, but they must report for the record in accordance with the regulations, and be subject to the control of fresh cocoon prices, and are not allowed to privately collect improved silkworm eggs.

Consistent with Jiangsu Province

The above points are comprehensively planned based on the situation of cocoon production in the province to ensure the adaptation of supply and demand in the province's silk factories and to promote unification and eliminate conflicts. This not only facilitates silkworm farmers in selling cocoons and maintaining the industry, but also serves the business of the association. Therefore, we submit this request, hoping that the government will review it and adopt it for the public good. Respectfully submitted to the Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, Huang.

Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau Changes Remittance Methods

Implementation Set for the First of Next Month

In order to facilitate the public and develop business, the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has reduced remittance fees and increased remittance amounts. In addition to this city, which has already implemented it, other cities will implement it on New Year's Day next year. The details are as follows:

Original Remittance Amount: The original remittance fee for postal savings remittances was half a cent per yuan within the province and one cent per yuan outside the province, with a minimum of five cents. The remittance amount ranged from one yuan to two thousand five hundred yuan.

Changes: Now, in order to develop business, facilitate the public, and reduce the burden on remitters, the bureau has reduced the remittance fees and increased the remittance amounts. Yesterday morning, Mr. Fang Tinghua, Director of the Remittances Department of the Postal and Remittance Bureau, told a China News Agency reporter that the current changes to the remittance methods involve changing the original remittance fee of half a cent per yuan within the province and one cent per yuan outside the province to a uniform rate, regardless of the province: five cents for remittances under five yuan, ten cents for remittances from five yuan to twenty yuan, two cents for remittances from twenty yuan to two hundred yuan, and one per thousand for remittances from two hundred yuan to ten thousand yuan (i.e., one yuan remittance fee per thousand yuan). The original remittance amount of two thousand five hundred yuan has also been increased to ten thousand yuan.

Phased Implementation: The above methods have been notified to the postal bureaus and instructed to comply. However, only the postal administration bureau and first-class postal bureaus can issue ten thousand yuan remittance slips. Except for Shanghai, which has already implemented it, other cities are scheduled to implement it starting on the first of next month.

After Landing, the Eurasia No. 16 Aircraft: Company Sends Workers to Repair

After On-Site Repair, the Aircraft Continues Its Flight Back to Shanghai

The Eurasia Aviation Corporation's No. 16 aircraft, which flew from Shaanxi to Shanghai on the 25th, was forced to land in the rice fields of Yin Village, Mochen Town, Changshu County, due to weather obstacles that evening. According to further news obtained from the company yesterday, after the aircraft was forced to land, the radio operator Hang Xiaozu remained at the scene to guard the No. 16 aircraft. The pilot, Schlieker, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon and reported to General Manager Li Jingcong. After hearing the situation, Li dispatched German mechanic Walter Glavin and Chinese mechanic Shen Yuanzhong and four workers with repair parts from Longhua Airport at 9 AM yesterday, traveling to Changshu by company truck to carry out repairs. Previously, it was planned to transport or dismantle all the aircraft parts and transport them to Shanghai. However, because the fuselage of the aircraft was not damaged and only the internal machinery was slightly damaged, and because the aircraft is a small, extremely fast, and stable aircraft, it was decided to repair it on site. Once repaired, it will continue its flight back to Shanghai. Because the aircraft's structure is better than others, it does not need to use wheels for takeoff, so it will not damage the crops in the rice fields.

The Warden of the Second Prison Pleads for the Prisoners Suffering from the Cold

Most of the Prisoners' Clothing and Bedding is Inadequate; Letter Sent to the Buddhist Laymen's Forest Seeking Donations

Due to the cold weather and approaching end of the year, most of the prisoners in the Jiangsu Second Prison on Route Ghisi (Xue Huili Road) are inadequately clothed and bedded, and their suffering from the cold is pitiful. Yesterday, Warden Hu Renqing sent a letter to the Buddhist Laymen's Forest in this city, requesting donations of clothing and bedding. The original letter is as follows: Respectfully, the number of prisoners in our prison is nearly three thousand, more than twice the fixed quota. They are poor and lack resources, and eight or nine out of ten are inadequately clothed and bedded. The weather is getting colder, and winter is approaching soon. The prisoners are suffering from the cold and are pitiful. The budget for clothing and bedding for prisoners in our prison is very small, and the national treasury is depleted, making funding extremely difficult. Using a cup of water to save a cartload of firewood will not solve the problem. We have long heard that great men generously help the masses, and all the world admires them. We hope that you will show mercy and extend your kindness to those in prison. Whether it is cotton clothes or quilts, please donate as much as possible so that those who are embracing their knees in prison can rely on your kindness to feel the warmth of spring. In this way, your benevolent acts will spread far and wide, like living Buddhas in ten thousand homes. If you agree, please let us know in advance so that we can send someone to collect them. We will be deeply grateful. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai World Buddhist Laymen's Forest, Hu Renqing, Warden of the Shanghai Jiangsu Second Prison.

The Little Actress Who Sang at the Tianyun Building Committed Suicide

She Was Only Fifteen Years Old; Unknown Reasons for Taking Poison

Xu Caifen, a girl from Chuansha, was fifteen years old and sang comic operas at the Tianyun Building of Wing On Company. She was quite famous and lived with her parents at No. 9, Lane 230, Xiamen Road. Unexpectedly, the girl suddenly had thoughts of ending her life for unknown reasons. She secretly swallowed opium and committed suicide. Her father, Xu Guiqing, discovered this and rushed her to the Pingmin Hospital on Route Tenant de la Tour. However, the treatment was ineffective, and she died at 6 AM the next morning. The hospital reported this to the Laozha patrol station in charge. Detective Wu Shoushan was instructed to investigate. He moved the body to the coroner's office on Rue Dunning. Yesterday morning, Zhang Zongru, a prosecutor appointed by the First Special District Local Court, visited the office to examine the body. Initially, Chinese Sergeant Lu Dagong reported the previous situation. Xu Guiqing, claiming to be forty-three years old and working on a ship, stated that the deceased was his daughter, who sang comic operas at Wing On Company, performing two shows a day, from 2:30 PM to 3:30 PM and from 7:30 PM to 8:15 PM. The day before yesterday, after the afternoon show, she told me that she would not be coming home for dinner that night. I did not suspect anything else, so I told her to bring more money to buy food. When she returned at about 9 PM that night, she went to bed. I asked her why, and she suddenly said that she had taken opium, but she refused to reveal what had stimulated her. After obtaining the statement, Zhang ruled that the deceased Xu Caifen was a woman who had died from opium poisoning during her lifetime. The body was released to her father, Xu Guiqing, who signed a statement to take it back for burial.

Shanghai Rural Township Chiefs Wire Request to Postpone Dredging of Hengli River

The township chiefs of the first and third districts of Shanghai County, in view of the long disrepair of the Hengli River and the siltation of the river, decided to start construction on January 5th next year to implement dredging work relief. However, because the beans and wheat planted by the villagers along the river have already grown, their losses would be great if they were sacrificed at once. The township chiefs requested the provincial authorities to postpone the work until the coming winter to prepare as early as possible in order to alleviate the people's hardship. The original telegram is as follows: Chairman Chen, Director Yu, Director Zhao, and Director Shen of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, Shanghai County will start construction on January 5th next year after having meetings in preparation of the dredging of Hengli River. Hengli River is a large river and dredging would take a long time. If construction starts now, it will inevitably hinder the spring plowing next year. The beans and wheat planted along the river are flourishing, and it would be a pity to sacrifice them. Moreover, this year's autumn harvest was very poor, and the people's strength cannot bear the burden. Therefore, we request that the government instruct Shanghai County to postpone the work and wait until the beginning of winter next year to prepare for it as early as possible so that there is sufficient time and no interference with farmland. Township Chief Yang Zhuoyun of Beiqiao Town, Third District of Shanghai County, township heads Zhang Shushan, Lin Quangen, He Zhaoxiong, Chuan Pingtu, Liu Wangshan, Township Chief Lin Kongjia of Yuqi Township, township heads Pan Jinshu respectfully.

Shareholder Lawsuit After the Closure of the Le Xiang Hotel

Sponsoring Shareholders Not Responsible for Losses: Li Yougeng's Lawsuit Adjudicated Yesterday

At the beginning of its operation, the Le Xiang Hotel on Jiujiang Road enjoyed a prosperous business with a full house of customers. Later, affected by the economic downturn, it gradually saw a decline in patrons and eventually closed down. The hotel owner, Hu Xiongsheng, when starting the business, created a special category of "sponsoring shares" to facilitate fundraising. It was stipulated that those who purchased sponsoring shares would not be liable for business losses and would receive a monthly dividend of one percent as a preferential treatment. Hu Xiongding, his brother, had a close friendship with Li Yougeng, a Hunanese man working in political circles, and persuaded Li to purchase twelve of these sponsoring shares, each worth five hundred dollars, totaling six thousand dollars. To secure his credibility, Hu Xiongding acted as a witness. Unexpectedly, after the hotel's closure, both Hus went into hiding one after the other. Although Li wanted to recover the share money based on the stock regulations, he was unable to negotiate. Therefore, he hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to file a lawsuit against the two Hus in the First Special District Court, requesting the court to order the defendants to repay the share money of five thousand nine hundred ninety-nine dollars, along with the statutory interest. The court, upon receiving the complaint, found that the defendants' addresses were unknown and there was no way to summon them. Therefore, it legally served a public notice, which has now expired. The court then allowed a one-sided debate. Lawyer Zhan presented the stock certificate and share book, which the presiding judge examined and clarified. The judgment was announced the day before yesterday, ordering the two defendants to repay the plaintiff five thousand nine hundred ninety-nine dollars, plus annual interest of five percent until the execution is completed, with the litigation costs to be borne by the defendants.

Wang Wanchun Convicted and Sentenced for Buying and Selling Silver Coins

Wang Wanchun, a native of Jiangbei who lives at 33 Huazhenfang, Xinjiang Road, Zhabei, and makes a living by renting out rickshaws, recently exchanged twenty yuan in paper money for twenty silver dollars from an elderly Cantonese woman, Li Yeshi, at the Central Bank's legal tender exchange office. Central Bank staff discovered this, arrested him, and handed him over to Chinese detective Sun Jishan, who took him to the General Police Station and then to the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang prosecuted him according to Articles 2 and 5 of the Ordinance on Obstructing National Currency. The court had summoned him several times. Because the court received a confidential letter reporting that Wang had previously pulled rickshaws for a foreigner, Wang's actions this time were instigated by someone else, intending to transport the silver dollars out of the country, etc. The court deemed it necessary to investigate this point and ordered Chinese Detective Chief Su Changsheng to investigate. Yesterday morning, when it was time for another hearing, Detective Su submitted his investigation report. When questioned, Wang continued to deny everything. After arguments between the police lawyer Wang and the defendant's lawyer, Qian Hongye, the presiding judge of the criminal court, announced the verdict in court: Wang Wanchun was sentenced to three years and six months imprisonment for exchanging silver coins with the intention of illegally exporting them, which was unsuccessful. The twenty yuan in paper money was confiscated.

Money Exchange Industry Decides to Immediately Exchange Legal Tender Upon Receipt. Tobacco Exchange Industry to Convene Agreement Meeting Tomorrow.

The Ministry of Finance, in order to prevent unscrupulous merchants from illegally exporting silver coins for profit, instructed the money exchange and tobacco exchange industries in this city to quickly formulate measures to suppress the private hoarding and selling of silver coins. After receiving the order, the respective industry associations notified their members to comply and discussed the suppression measures, submitting them to the Ministry of Finance for review. The Real News Agency reporter investigated and recorded the following details:

Money Exchange Industry Reply to Money Industry Association

After receiving the Ministry's order, the Money Industry Association immediately notified its 54 member stores and non-member small money exchanges to comply. It also sent letters to the Money Exchange Industry Tongyi Association and the Tobacco Exchange Industry Association, urging them to quickly formulate suppression measures. According to inquiries, the Money Exchange Industry has replied to the Money Industry Association, stating that since the Ministry of Finance implemented the monetary policy on November 4th, all hard currency of the 40 member stores has been exchanged for legal tender in accordance with the order. Hereafter, any incoming hard currency will be immediately exchanged. Regarding the Ministry's order, a meeting of the industry was convened yesterday to discuss and decide to reply to your association. We hope that you will take note of this.

Tobacco Exchange to Convene an Agreement Meeting

Although the Tobacco Exchange Industry Association made a resolution at a general meeting the day before yesterday to thoroughly handle the case of suppressing the private hoarding and selling of silver coins, the suppression measures have not yet been finalized. In order to implement sanctions against private hoarders and sellers as soon as possible, it has specially notified wholesale merchants among its members to convene an emergency meeting of all agreement members at 2:00 PM on the 29th (Sunday) to discuss and formulate suppression measures for submission to the executive supervisory committee for review and implementation. Investigation into Li Zifeng's Suicide by Poison

Li Zifeng, a native of Ningbo, thirty-five years old, was formerly an accountant at the Guohua Printing Press. Recently unemployed, he had relatives living at number 7, Lane 5, Ximen Road, French Concession. A week ago, the relatives moved to an old house in Lane 5 of the Hongkou district, leaving behind furniture and other items that had not been completely moved. Therefore, they asked Li Zifeng to stay at number 7, Lane 5 to look after the place. On the afternoon of the 25th, at around 3:00 PM, the rickshaw puller of his relatives, Yuan Zilong from Jiangbei, went to visit and found Li lying on his bed, looking weak and exhausted. Suspecting he was ill, Yuan immediately took him to Guangci Hospital by rickshaw. After examination by the doctor, it was discovered that Li had committed suicide by poison. When asked about the reason, Li was unable to speak and the cause of death remained unclear. Eventually, due to the deep poisoning, the treatment was ineffective and he died at 10:00 PM that night. The hospital reported to the police, who sent the body in a vehicle to the Tongren Funeral Hall for examination. His elderly father, Li Yinsheng, sixty-one years old, rushed to Shanghai from his hometown after hearing the news. Yesterday, he reported the matter to the Second Special District Court. Prosecutor Wang Ren arrived at the hall and confirmed that the deceased had indeed died from poison taken before death. The body was handed over to his father for burial with a written guarantee.
